CHINA
SEED SECTOR COMMERCIALIZATION PROJECT
PLANTER BOX SEED SURVEYS
PURPOSE
The purpose of the "Planter Box Seed Surveys" is to survey the quality of seeds of selected
crops saved by farmers for planting (the so-called informal seed sector) and to compare the
quality of the farmer-saved seeds with that of seeds of the same kind and variety available
in the market.
GENERAL PROCEDURE
The surveys will be made at planting time for the selected crops so that information on seeds
actually being planted can be obtained along with a small sample for analysis and testing.
CROP SEED KINDS SURVEYED
Wheat, soybean and/or conventional rice, i.e., non-hybrid. These are important crops of the
self-pollinated type for which seed saving by farmers is a common practice worldwide. It
might be difficult to find a suitable area for surveying where conventional rice is planted by
a sufficient portion of farmers for convenient survey. If this turns out to be the case, the
focus should be on wheat and soybean. Soybean is included because the seeds are more
difficult for farmers to save with good maintenance of quality than most other seed kinds.
On the other hand, seeds of rice are perhaps the easiest seeds to save with good maintenance
of quality. Shandong province is recommended for soybean; Henan for wheat.
SURVEY AREAS
Representative counties in Shandong (soybean) and Henan (wheat) provinces for each of the
two seed kinds to be surveyed should be selected and within each county, one or more
villages with a population of several hundred farmers to provide for a good sample of 100
farmers in the field planting during the planting season. The survey would be repeated in
the same or an adjacent county the following season in the same manner to provide two 100
farmer samples for each seed kind for total of 200 farmers.
SURVEY PERIOD AND NUMBERS
- 2 seed kinds (wheat and soybean or conventional rice)
- 2 years
- 100 farmers per kind per year
- 2 seed kinds (areas) x 2 years x 100 farmers/survey = 400 farmers.
400 farmers = 400 samples



- 87 -                                 Annex 2
Page 2 of 3
ORGANIZATION, COLLABORATION AND RESPONSIBILITIES
The surveys should be under the general sponsorship of the Project Management Office in
association with the Provincial PMO of the Province or Provinces selected for the surveys.
The Provincial Seed Administration(s) or Seed Administrations of the Prefecturate(s) in which
the counties to be surveyed are located should be responsible for the surveys with a qualified
person assigned as Survey Leader. Collaboration should be established with the major seed
company in the area and with the Agrotechnical Extension Centers to assist with selection
of the survey areas, accompany and assist the surveyors, provide transportation and be
helpful in other ways..
- Personnel of the Provincial or Prefectural Seed Stations would   &x'J te
farmers, obtain the desired information and collect samples. Transportation
would be provided by the pertinent Administration.
- The Provincial or Prefectural Seed Testing Laboratory would make the
purity and germination analyses of the samples collected. To the extent
possible, the purity analyses would include an assessment of varietal purity
as well as physical purity, and observations on seed health would be made
during the purity analysis and germination test.
- The Agrotechnical Extension Center would be responsible for planting out
the samples in the field for additional observations on varietal purity.
SURVEY PROCEDURES AND EVALUATIONS
- Two to four person team would move through survey area during planting
season for the crop, identify farmers actually planting the crop or making
preparations to plant in the next several days, obtain specified information
from the farmer and a sample of the seeds that are or will be planted. The
size of seed sample will be 1 kg and the seeds will be replaced with clean.
good quality seeds of the same variety. The farmer will be asked to plant the
replacment seeds in one location and mark the location with bamboo poles
with cloth "flags" at the beginning and end of the replacement seeds.
- The information collected from each farmer surveyed would be relatively
brief and simple: name and location of field (for followup visit); number of
mu to be planted; seeding rate per mu; the variety and source of seed (where
did he get the seeds he is planting?, saved himself, from neighbor, from seed
company, from extenstion center, other); why did he choose the
source of seed that he chose?; why did he choose the variety that is being planted?
- The 1 kg samples would be taken at to the seed testing laboratory that will
do the work and divided into two 500 g samples. One sample would be used



- 88 -                                  Annex 2
Page 3 of 3
for purity, germination and other laboratory tests; the other sample would be
used for the field planting. The laboratory tests would be made using
standard procedures with the additional assessments and observations on
varietal purity and seed health as mentioned above. The field tests would be
only for obervations on varietal purity and consist of duplicate rows of each
sample, 125 -150 seeds per row thinned in seedling stage to approximately
100 plants. Row and plant spacing would be closer than for VCU testing.
Varietally pure seeds of each variety represented in the survey (obtained from
foundation seed stocks) would be planted in the row before and after the
survey rows. The field plantings would be evaluated several times to
determine variety purity and make observations on specific diseases.
- Followup visits would be made to 25 of the farmers surveyed to observe the
performance of the varietally pure, processed and good quality seeds that
replaced the seeds taken in the sample.
- The survey leader would assemble the results of the laboratory analyses and
field evaluations, categorize the samples according to source of seeds (i.e.,
home-saved, neighbor, seed company, seed station, other) and make
appropriate comparisions of quality among the sources of seeds surveyed.
Additional data for analysis and comparison could be obtained from
laboratory test results of samples of seeds of the same variety for seeds
marketed in the county or prefecturate by seed companies and seed stations.
REQUIREMENTS
The requirements for the surveys would not be great. For an extension effort of these sorts,
personnel time ought to be assigned. The remaining requirements would be: transportation
costs for the survey; seeds from seed companies operating in the area of the different
varieties encountered to replace the 1 kg sample taken from farmer; laboratory supplies and
materials for testing; use of equipment, materials and field plots for field tests. An adequate
and reasonable budget for essential requirements would be about Y160 per sample. For the
two years of the survey, 2 crops, and 100 samples/crop/year, the budget would be:
100 samples x 2 crops x 2 years x 160 = Y64.000 (maximum, it could  be nuch
less depending on cooperators & cooperation.



AnngX 3
Page 1 of 7
- 89 -
CHINA
SEED SECTOR COMMERCIALIZATION PROJECT
PILOT COMPANIES FOR COMMERCIALIZATION
1.        In order tc establish company structures which could serve as models
for the commercialization of the Chinese seed sector, 3 pilot companies were
identified which will be monitored closely throughout the implementation phase
of the Project. The 3 pilot companies are based on current operations of (i) a
state farm, (ii) a prefecture seed company, and (iii) a provincial seed company.
These companies will be formed as limited liability companies or limited
liability stock companies under Chinese Company laws as adopted in December 29,
1993. Operationally, these companies will be structured quite differently and
are intended to serve as examples for other entities pursuing the objective of
commercialization. Under the Project it is proposed that these pilot companies
be provided with additional training and technical assistance to ensure
successful conversion to commercialized operations. Monitoring procedures have
been identified to ensure that these companies will accomplish their objectives.
Zhangqiu State Farm
2.        Zhangqiu State Farm (ZSF) is located in the Zhangqiu Prefecture in
Shandong Province: ZSF operates on about 8,000 mu (530 ha), half of which is used
for the production of grain. The state farm recently concluded an exclusive
agreement with the Zhangqiu Municipal Leek Research Institute (ZMLRI) for the
representation of new varieties. ZMLRI is the only institute in China involved
in the development of new varieties of leek. All leek seed grown commercially in
China today is hybrid seed.
3.        ZSF originally proposed to operate the seed business as a separate
division of the state farm; subsequent to several reviews, however, it was
decided that the seed business be spun off the state farm operations and
established as a limited liability company, Zhangqiu Leek Seed Company (ZLSC).
This company will assume the licensing agreement with ZMLRI and will be
responsible for the production and marketing of foundation and commercial seed.
ZLSC will contract for all of its seed production requirements; while ZSF will
be a preferred seed producer due to its longstanding experience with the
production of high quality leek seed, production will also be contracted with
other seed producers to ensure a competitive environment. Foundation seed will
be marketed under licensing arrangements and commercial seed will be marketed
either direct or through representatives in other provinces.
4.        Annually China produces leek on about 267,000 ha; at planting rates
of 7.5 kg/ha this requires about 2,000 t of commercial seed. This commercial seed
can be produced on about 2,600 ha (seed yields of 750 kg/ha) which requires about
20 t of foundation seed (7.5 kg/ha). At foundation seed yields of about 380
k-/ha, 20 t can be produced on about 50 ha. Under the Project, ZLSC plans to
market about 20 t of foundation seed annually and to increase sales of commercial
seed to about 700 t over 5 years.
5.        Leek seed will be the primary product of ZLSC; however, in order to
have a minimum of diversification, the company will also market celery seed
(about 100 t/year) and radish seeds (about 200 t/year) under agreements with the
Institute for Vegetable Seeds in Shandong.
6.        As ZLSC will be created as a limited liability company with a minimum
of two initial shareholders. Chinese law required limited liability companies
and limited liability stock companies to be supervised by a Board of Directors.
This board will be composed of one representative each of ZLSC, ZSF, ZMLRI,
Zhangqiu City Seed Cc-.pany, and a contract seed producer. Management will report



An3
- 90 -                            Page 2 of 7
to this board as management in a shareholding company would report to the board
of directors.
7.        The general manager of the company will be assisted by two deputies;
one being responsible for finance and sales/marketing, the other responsible for
seed production and conditioning. The quality assurance function as well as
support services will report directly to the general manager. Total company staff
will be approximately 50.
8.        Of critical importance for the company will be the supply of new,
improved germplasm on a regular basis. In the past, release of new varieties in
China was rather slow; research institutes constantly made improvements to once
released varieties, but they did not change the designation of the product. This
policy resulted in the fact that varieties marketed today do no longer truly
resemble the characteristics of the original product but they are still marketed
under the designation of that original product. This situation will change with
the introduction of plant breeders' rights (PBR). - In its negotiations with
ZMLRI, ZLSC will ensure that new varieties will be available on a regular basis.
ZMLRI will have the responsibility to describe these varieties and to obtain
protection under PBR; ZLSC will have the responsibility to ensure varietal purity
so that the product which is marketed truly reflects the characteristics as
described by ZMLRI. ZLSC will pay a license fee (royalty) to ZMLRI for the right
to produce and market the products developed by the institute, and this license
will be established as a percentage of the price for which ZLSC sells its seed.
This arrangement will significantly change the marketing of seeds; ZLSC will
regularly launch new products into the market, they will have to manage "product
cycles" including the phasing out of products on the decline.
9.        In its seed production operations,  ZLSC will  have to negotiate
contracts which take into account the actual cost of production incurred by the
producers plus a small premium for their efforts to produce seed as compared to
a commercial crop. Superior quality should demand a higher premium. However, as
sales prices for seed will remain rather low in comparison with world market
prices for a number of years, it is of utmost importance for all seed companies
that they control their seed production cost and attempt to keep them as low as
possible. Only this policy will allow them to make a reasonable profit from their
operations which can then be reinvested into the business (including research).
10.       ZLSC intends to market its seed through 4 sales points within the
prefecture as well as through representatives/agents in other regions. One major
customer will be Zhangqiu City Seed Company which already today sells several
hundred tons of leek seed to provinces such as Liaoning, Anhui, Henan, Shanxi,
and others. A brand image and identity for Zhangqiu leek seed has been
established. ZLSC must ensure that it uses this brand identity to its advantage
while creating its own identity for seed of superior quality. ZLSC will have to
segment its markets, particularly in regards to the sale of foundation vs.
commercial seed; and ZLSC must very carefully select the customers to whom they
sell foundation seed to ensure that the high quality of its foundation seed is
maintained in the commercial seed produced by these customers.
11.       ZLSC will eutablish its own company internal quality assurance program
to ensure that these quality issues are being observed. Thus the quality
assurance department has a responsibility not only for the seed produced by the
company but also must, from time to time, check the seed produced by the
company's licensees. The quality standards established by this quality assurance
program will be superior to those established in the official government
regulations.
12.       Significant training and technical assistance will be provided for
ZLSC to ensure that management is equipped with the knowledge and understanding
for the company to accomplish its objectives. Also, monitoring procedures and
performance indicator- have been identified to measure the companies progress.



- 91 -                            PageT-of 7
These will be explained in the summary section.
ZiBo Prefecture Seed Company
13.       ZiBo Prefecture Seed Company (ZPSC) is located in the city of ZiBo in
Shandong province. The company operates with a staff of 50 people, it maintains
a central office and seed cleaning facility, a research farm, and 6 retail stores
in the municipality of ZiBo. All management staff of ZPSC are agronomists,
holding the responsibilities of (i) general manager, also responsible for
finance, (ii) vegetable seed sales manager, (iii) wheat and corn sales manager,
(iv) manager for buildings/services/engineering, (v) research and production
manager.
14.       ZPSC developed its proposal for participation in the Project based on
an in-house research program for chinese cabbage and the recent acquisition of
the production and marketing rights to a corn hybrid. The company suggests that
the functions and responsibilities of the seed station have already been
separated from its operations; this is yet to be verified. The company intends
to continue operating as a stand-alone operation but to increase its market share
in hybrid corn and to expand interregional marketing of vegetable seeds.
15.        ZPSC will be established as a limited liability company, as with
Zhangqiu, the company will have at least two shareholders; and it was suggested
to offer a minority interest also to the managers. Management will report to a
Board of Directors whose members will represent the shareholders as well as
successful local businesses.   The land and buildings which the company will
operate will be transferred to the company by transfer of a "right to use".
These rights will be valued as equity contributions by the shareholders to the
capital stock of the company; and the transfer of these rights will be signed off
on by local government to ensure that management is autonomous in deciding on the
use of these land and buildings.
16.       The general manager will report directly to the Board of Directors;
he will be assisted by three deputies responsible for (i) seed production and
conditioning, (ii) research, foundation seed production, and variety testing,
(iii) marketing and sales of seed of Chinese cabbage and hybrid corn. The finance
department, the quality assurance department, and the support services will
report directly to the general manager. Total company staff will be about 50.
17.       In vegetable seeds, ZPSC has about 1,400 accessions of Chinese cabbage
as its proprietary germplasm pool; the research effort is directed towards the
development of hybrids. Total cost of the research program is about 300,000 Yuan
per year. While the company considers its genetic basis as sufficient and its
hybrids superior as regards quality and earliness, ZPSC will change its products
release policy as described above for Zhangqiu, including protection of new
varieties under PBR. ZPSC will also begin significant efforts to identify other
sources for improved germplasm nationally and internationally. These products
would be secured for the company either through licensing operations or
otherwise.
18.       In corn  seeds  ZPSC  will  also  actively  pursue  new  sources  for
germplasm. Presently the company has a production and marketing right to one corn
hybrid developed by Shandong Agricultural Research Institute; under the project
the company will explore both national and international breeders for improved
products.
19.       Concerning seed production, ZPSC will produce all foundation seed of
Chinese cabbage and hybrid corn on its own research farm; the technical and
management expertise to carry out this production has already been established.
Production of commercial seed will be contracted out. The seed production system
in the ZiBo prefecture is such that adequate isolation for the production of high



- 92 -                             Annex 3
Page 4 of 7
quality seed of different varieties can be guaranteed through contracts with
farm-households.
20.        ZPSC presently sells about 150 t of cabbage seeds annually, 15 t in
the regional market and 135 t in the interregional market; at this level the
company is not able to meet market demand. ZPSC projects to increase sales to
about 500 t/year. This increase will be accomplished through an expansion of the
existing network of representatives/agents throughout China (this network
currently extends over 25 provinces throughout the country). ZPSC has already
established a proprietary package for "ZiBo Cabbage Seed" which clearly
distinguishes it from any other source; this package also has created a brand
image for the company in the interregional market. The company will accomplish
its sales objectives by building on and expanding this brand identity. - ZPSC
presently sells its corn seeds within the prefecture; the company recently
concluded contractual arrangements with 6 county seed companies to sell ZPSC corn
seeds exclusively under the Project. ZPSC will also pursue sales opportunities
outside the prefecture, most likely through some of its vegetable seed dealers.
Following this strategy the company should accomplish its projected sales
increase of corn seeds from 500 t to 5,000 t annually.
21.       ZPSC will establish and strengthen its own company internal quality
assurance program to ensure that the highest possible seed quality is produced
and sold. As the acreage to carry out the projected production will be rather
large, the company will work with local staff in the various seed production
communities which are not permanent employees but supervise production on account
of and according to the standards of the company.   The quality standards
implemented by the company will be superior to the standards established for the
external governmental quality control inspections.
22.       Significant training and technical assistance will be provided for
ZLSC to ensure that management is equipped with the knowledge and understanding
for the company to accomplish its objectives. Also, monitoring procedures and
performance indicators have been identified to measure the companies progress.
These will be explained in the summary section.
Guangxi Provincial Seed Company
23.       Guangxi Provincial Seed Company  (GSC) is located in Nanning,  the
capital of Guangxi Province; with 83 million people this province is the third
most populated province of China. Until 1995 GPSC still operated much according
to the old hierarchical system; it was the supplier of breeder seed to most
prefecture seed companies in the province and the official quality control
laboratory was still managed by GSC.  However, as a participant in the ASSP
project the provincial government plans to accomplish the establishment of an
official laboratory outside GSC by late 1995 or early 1996; buildings have been
constructed and they are awaiting delivery of the laboratory equipment.
24.       There are 97 seed companies in the province; the provincial seed
company, 13 prefecture seed companies, and 83 county seed companies. A number of
the prefecture and county companies have already moved to a more commercialized
system and are marketing seed in the interregional trade. GSC originally intended
to form a group company with 3 prefecture seed companies and 11 county seed
companies to participate in the Project. This, however, would not have
accomplished the desired consolidation and efficiencies as every participant
would have desired to continue and expand its seed production activity. It was
therefore decided and agreed to form a limited liability stock company on the
basis of GSC with participation of 5 county seed companies.
25.        The newly formed company (GPSC) will have a group of shareholders,
electing a Board of Directors, appointing a chairman of the Board, and through
this structure superv Lse the management of the company.  The company will be



- 93 -                            Page 5 of 7
managed by a general manager who would not be a member of the board; this general
manager would be assisted by 3 deputies. One deputy general manager will be
responsible for seed production and conditioning, one for sales and marketing,
and one for finance/administration.  Service functions, the quality assurance
department and evaluation of new products will report directly to the general
manager.
26.       The company will operate from its central location in Nanning where
it also maintains its foundation seed farm; away from this center there will be
5 seed production locations and one sales office at the border with Vietnam. The
production locations will be at PingGuo (Corn), HePu (peanuts and kenaf
[dogbane]), and BeiLiu, HeXian, and TianYong (hybrid rice).
27.       The shareholders will contribute to the company the right to use
certain facilities for the production of seeds; the 5 seed conditioning lines
will be installed at these facilities. The shareholders will also make available
to GPSC certain personnel during the harvest and conditioning season to allow the
company to manage its seed crop and to keep its permanent staff at a minimum.
GPSC, however, will have, through its own staff, supervisory responsibility of
all seed production operations and will also have the responsibility to service
and maintain the seed processing lines.   The number of shares held by each
shareholder will be determined after the value of the facilities to be
contributed has been established.
28.       Great responsibility will lie with the department for the evaluation
of new varieties as none of the companies joining into GPSC has any proprietary
products or research programs or holds any licenses to such products.   GPSC
therefore must urgently obtain new varieties for testing from both national and
international sources and evaluate them at multiple locations throughout the
province as well as in the interregional markets. GPSC has been put in contact
with potential international sources for new varieties and the implementation of
an accelerated testing program for such new products will be one of the benchmark
by which this company will be evaluated.
29.       In structuring GPSC it was ensured that the strongest of the initial
14 candidates for participation in the group company were selected for the new
shareholding company; the intent being that some of the seed production
operations of the other companies will become superfluous. These companies would
then become agents and/or representatives of the company for marketing its seed
products. Initial discussions on this concept have been held with a number of
these companies; this, however, can be accomplished successfully only if GPSC
proves that it is in a position to supply superior products from a standpoint of
genetics and mechanical quality at competitive prices.
30.       GPSC will establish its own internal quality assurance department and
laboratory; GPSC also will establish a seed quality assurance program and
standards to be met. These standards will be above those issued by the official
government control offices.   A significant task will be to ensure uniform
implementation of these standards at all five production/processing locations.
This too will be a benchmark by which GPSC will be evaluated throughout the
implementation of the project.   In order to assist this effort, GPSC will
establish small laboratories for quick analyses directly at the processing sites;
all seed prepared for sale, however, will have to be checked by the central
laboratory in Nanning before that seed can be sold.
31.       In rice, Guangxi province produces about 2.5 million ha per year
annually in two crops; first crop is planted in January and harvested in June,
second crop is planted in July and harvested in December.  Thus the time for
harvesting/processing a seed crop is extremely short if companies have to operate
without carryover seed. Today about 70% of all rice is hybrid; it is projected
that by the year 2000 this will have increased to about 85%. At planting rates
of 22.5 kg/ha this wiil require about 47,000 t of seed annually. GPSC projects



- 94 -                            Annex 3
Page 6 of 7
to supply about 16,000 t of hybrid rice seed by the year 2000, representing a
market share of about 21%; however, a significant quantity will also be sold into
the interregional market and to Vietnam. This can be accomplished with hybrids
of superior performance and seed of superior quality.
32.       In corn, Guangxi province produces about 530,000 ha annually, 45% of
which is hybrid; it is projected that the use of hybrid seed will increase to
about 80% by the year 2000. Planting rates, however, should decrease from the
current 45 kg/ha to about 35 kg/ha, resulting in annual seed needs of about
13,000 t. GPSC plans to accomplish sales of about 6,200 t by the year 2000,
representing a market share of about 48%. The company plans to accomplish this
objective primarily through the improvement of seed quality, thus allowing the
farmer to reduce his planting rates; longterm, however, the company also must
distinguish itself by offering improved varieties.
33.       Guangxi province produces about 190,000 ha of peanuts annually; at
planting rates of 225 kg and a four year seed replacement rate, this results in
annual seed needs of about 10,700 t. It is projected that the seed replacement
rate will change to three years as GPSC will provide a superior product to the
farmers; this scenario makes the sales projection of 4,000 t for the year 2000
attainable.
34.       In kenaf, the province produces about 4,000 t of seed annually which
is mostly sold into the interregional markets. GPSC targets a sales volume of
about 3,000 t for the year 2000, primarily by being able to replace other
producers which cannot compete with GPSC's seed quality.
35.       The buildup of a strong, customer oriented marketing and distribution
network will be a prerequisite for GPSC to accomplish its sales objectives. The
company will  build  on the  contacts  which  its  shareholders  have  already
established in the interregional markets and consolidate these, it will introduce
its own brand, and it will use it close relations with county seed companies to
supply its superior products in their markets.  Significant market research
however will have to be done to identify competitor's strengths and weaknesses
and to identify market niches.
36.       Significant training and technical assistance will be provided for
GPSC to ensure that management is equipped with the knowledge and understanding
for the company to accomplish its objectives. Also, monitoring procedures and
performance indicators have been identified to measure the companies progress.
These will be explained in the summary section.
Summary
37.       Training and technical assistance for the three pilot companies will
be coordinated to meet their needs. Foreign training will be provided for general
business management, marketing, and seed quality; local training will also be
provided for the afore mentioned as well as for finance, production, and seed
plant operations. The accomplishment of these training schedules throughout the
implementation phase of the project will be one of the performance indicators by
which these companies will be measured during supervision. Technical assistance
in the above indicated fields will be provided throughout the first two years of
operation.
38.       All companies were provided with guidelines for statutes and charters
for the establishment of these companies as legal, autonomous entities; draft
documents are to be submitted to the Bank prior to negotiation of the Loan. While
the company structures as described above appear to be satisfactory, it must yet
be ensured that these autonomous structures can actually operate autonomously
following implementation of the Project and this will be monitored closely during
supervision.



Annex 3
Page 7 of 7
39.       All companies also must supply documentation that certain property on
which the seed processing facilities are to be constructed have been transferred
to these companies for their exclusive use and that no authority can dictate to
these enterprises to alter the intended use or to infringe on it.
40.       In  order  to  prepare  the  pilot  companies  for  a  competitive,
commercialized environment, they were directed to minimize their spending on
social services and to substitute this with higher salaries/wages. The practice
of job guarantee is to be discontinued, housing should not be provided by the
companies, and the companies are to implement the practice of hiring temporary
workers during the peak seasons so that permanent employment and the related
expenses can be minimized.
41.       Management auconomy will be measured by the ability of company
management to establish prices, production targets, purchasing and selling
policies, engage in *he import and export of seeds, decide on investments,
acquire and transfer assets, establish joint ventures, hire and dismiss
employees, manage personnel and set wages and bonuses, and decide on the use of
retained earnings.
42.       In addition to the above outlined, certain performance indicators were
developed by which the companies will be evaluated during the implementation
phase of the project. These are:
- Obtaining certificates concerning the legal status of the companies
and documentation for transfer of assets;
- Adhering to the project implementation schedules;
- Establishing a system of monitoring expenditures and commitments
during project implementation by the time of the project launch workshop;
- Achieving training objectives according to schedules;
- Establishing company internal quality standards prior to the first
seed production season;
- Realizing production and sales volumes according to the 5 year
schedules; and
- Accomplishing the per unit profit margins which were established in
the financial calculations by setting prices according to market conditions and
controlling production costs accordingly.

CHINA
SEED SECTOR COMMERCIALIZATION PROJECT
Performance Indicators
1.        The major objective of this project is to assist the government in
developing a viable commercial seed sector, which can not only produce high
quality seeds in sufficient quantity and variety to satisfy farmers, needs but
also operates through efficient, self-sustained commercial enterprises.   The
project would assist in the commercialization of the seed sector (a) by helping
the government establish a seed policy and a regulatory framework that would
provide a conducive environment to enhance the competitiveness of the seed sector
and to encourage international cooperation, (b) by assisting in strengthening
institutions so that they can provide effective service and technical support to
the seed sector and (c) by supporting the modernization and rationalization of
selected seed companies.
2.        To measure progress made in implementation of the project, important
performance indicators were developed for the policy and regulatory,
institutional strengthening and commercialization components during  project
preparation (Annex 7 Table 1). These indicators, would be used to evaluate the
progress of the project and, if necessary, to redesign the project during the
mid-term review.
Policy and Reaulatorv Component:
3.        Seed Sector Policy.  The MOA is drafting a seed sector policy as part
of the National Seed Sector Industrialization Program. The policy aim to (a)
establish a modernized seed sector; (b) separate seed administration from seed
commercialization; (c) establish an integrated system of production and
marketing; (d) change in seed company structure to independent units; (e) open
up markets for interprovincial and international trade; and (f) relax price
control. The final draft of this seed sector policy would be submitted to the
State Council by the end of 1996.
4.        Seed Law.  The draft seed law is being revised and the seed law
drafting group estimates that the new seed law will be ready for submitting to
the State Council by the end of 1996.
5.        Reform and revision will be made to the following areas:
. the varietal registration and release procedure
. provisions for labelling seed for sale with seed
quality parameters
. inspection procedures for labelling for provincial external
quality control agencies
. provisions for voluntary seed certification schemes
. provisions affecting seed marketing, including the licensing of
seed marketers.
6.        Membership in International Organizations.  To commercialize the seed
sector, to improve the quality of seed stock and to encourage international
cooperation and trade, China needs to be a member of international seed
organizations. The two major organizations are the International Union for the
Protection of the New Varieties (UPOV) and International Seed Testing Association
(ISTA). It is required that a country must have acceptable plant breeder rights



Annex 7
- 140 -                           Table 2 of 5
(PBR) legal framework before joining UPOV. It is also required that ISTA testing
and laboratory utandards have to be adopted. Substantial work has already been
carried out to satisfy these requirements; the initial draft of PBR legislation
has been completed and reviewed with experts from UPOV and ISTA. In general,
this draft contains the regulations required for conformity with the requirements
of UPOV. The next steps for further action are as follows:
7.        UPOV. The drafting group for the PBR legal framework will revise the
current draft of the regulations, after unofficial advice from UPOV, to ensure
that it conforms with the provisions of the 1978 Act of the Convention. A draft
apparently conforming to the 1978 Act will then be submitted to the Council of
UPOV for advice on conformity. Following informal advice of conformity by the
Council, the responsible agency of the Government will seek formal advice from
the Council on conformity.
8.        The organizations represented on the drafting group will agree on the
location, staffing and financing of the PBR office; draft and pass into law
implementing regulations for the operation of the office; and draw up and
officially publish a list of species to be initially included under the PBR
legislation.   Then the responsible agency of Government will forward the
instrument of accession to the UPOV Council for approval.
9.        ISTA  The Seed Testing Division (STD) will continue to negotiate with
ISTA to resolve the issues that are preventing the Division from forwarding the
application for membership and authorization to issue ISTA international
certificates. STD will work on these issues and forward the application to ISTA
by the end of 1996, if the issues are resolved.
Institutional Strenathenina Component.
10.       Seed Oualitv Laboratories.   Site selection, design of facilities,
commencement of construction, and procurement of the equipment for the seed
quality testing laboratories in the official quality control agencies and seed
companies, will be initiated in the first year of the project. Prior to use of
the laboratory facilities, all laboratories will obtain copies of the official
rules for seed testing and adequately train staff in their use.
11.       External and Internal Oualitv Control Separation.  Prior to the start
of the project all provinces participating in the project will ensure the
separation, in both resources and finances, of their agencies for official
external seed quality control from the internal quality control programs of the
seed companies.
12.       Training.  Training of staff for both external and internal quality
control will take place equally in Years 1 and 2 of the project.
13.       Variety Evaluation Office Facilities.  The computers and accessories
for the National Variety Evaluation and Registration office. and the small cold
seed store specified will be procured in the first year of the project.
14.       Ouality Manaaement Workshoios. Workshops to evaluate the impact of the
operation of PBR and the seed quality management systems initiated in the project
will be organized in the Year 3 and undertaken in Years 4 and 5 of the project.
15.       Informal Sector.  Two planter box surveys of the quality of seed in
the informal seed sector, i.e., seeds saved by farmers or obtained from close
neighbors for planting, will be initiated in the first year of the project. The
results would be used by the seed companies and the agro-extension stations in
improving the quality of conventional seeds. It is expected that by the year
2005, the yield of conventional seeds would be increased by at least 10%.



Annex 7
- 141 -                            page 3 of 5
Commercialization Comoonent:
16.       Each seed enterprise would develop a Project Key Activities Schedule,
which in a bar chart schedule showing key indicators for monitoring project
progress (Figure 2). The first year of the project would include establishment
of facilities, training of enterprise and project managers and preparation of
bidding documents. Some seed production could begin during the first project
year, particularly the procurement and propagation of new genetic materials. The
majority of civil construction works and equipment procurement would be completed
during the second project year, with processing facilities being commissioned
before the end of the year.  Some project seeds could therefore be processed
late in the second year, but most processing and storage systems would not be
available for use until the third project year.
17.       Production, processing and marketing of seeds has been planned to
begin in project year two with 25% production, increasing to 50% in project year
three and 75% and 100% in years four and five respectively.  The production
schedules of some individual enterprises vary slightly from this average
schedule, particularly those of enterprises producing seedlings, which wouldhave
no sales until project year three.
18.       The progress of each enterprise would be evaluated according to the
Implementation plan set out in its Key Activities Schedule (Figure 2).
19.       In addition, enterprise performance would be evaluated according to
the following points:
(a)  Management.  Have the certificates of legal status of companies and
documentation for transfer of assets been obtained? Does the manager
have autonomy over in management of the business?         -
(b)  Production Targets.   Production and sales will be evaluated  in
comparison to annual targets over a 5-year period.  It is expected
that by the year 2005, there will be 15% increase in improved seeds
available to farmers.
(c) InterDrovincial and International Trade. Number of transactions and
quantity of sales to other provinces and other countries. By the year
2005, 30% of seed produced would be traded interprovincially.
(d)  Profits   Per-unit profit margins will be evaluated for adequacy.
Have prices been set according to market conditions, and have
production costs been controlled?
(o)  Cash Manaaement.   Has a system  for monitoring expenditures and
commitments been established during project implementation prior to
the time of the project launch workshop?
(f)  Trainin.   Have training objectives  been achieved  according to
schedules?
(g)  Oualitv Assurance.   Have company internal quality standards been
established prior to the first seed production season?
Additional Indicators.
20.       Additional indicators were developed to monitor the impact of the
project in the commercial seed sector and the farm sector as follows:
(a) Commercial Sectc: How many seed companies have achieved the objective of
becoming efficient, *E.f-uustained and profitable commercial enterprises?  How

many new companies outside th- project have adopted the style of development
initiated under the project? How active is domestic and international trade in
seed? It in expected that in the Year 2005, at least 50 seed companies would
achieve  full commercialization.   At  least 20 international  joint v-nture
companies would have business in China.
(b) Farm sector: What percentage of hybrid and improved conventional *sede are
used in crop production?   What does the comparison of incremental yield,
production and income of farmers in the project areas compared to the situation
before the project *how? How much have grain production and farmers' incom
increased?

CHINA
SEED SECTOR COMMERCIALIZATION PROJECT
Terms of Reference
International Seed Industry Lead Consultant
Location.       Beijing with some field travel.
Duration.       Two months, one month during each visit.
One month for the workshop.
oualifications: The consultant should have formal qualification in agriculture
or plant sciences and should have extensive working experience
in several countries in seed industry including seed
technology, variety testing and release, field inspection and
certification and seed testing. The consultant should have
working experience in an International Seed Testing
Association (ISTA) accredited seed testing station. Working
experience in Chinese seed regulations is essential.
Duties:         Working in cooperation with the Director of the Central PMO,
and Seed Division and the Director of the National
Agricultural Extension and Services Center for Seed, the
consultant shall:
- act as the International Lead Consultant for the preparation
and implementation of the Seed Sector Commercialization
Project including identification of international consultants
for the seed regulation and seed enterprise management
component.
- assist DOA in the preparation of the seed quality assurance
implementation system which covers both variety release and
official and internal control that is in accordance with the
recent institutional restructuring in China, recommendations
and supports under the project.
- supervise the implementation of the project seed quality
assurance component including development of official seed
stations and seed company internal quality control
laboratories.
- design courses to be implemented both by the international
and Chinese consultants according to Chinese requirement on
variety release, field inspection, seed testing and seed
certification and have them endorsed by the Ministry of
Agriculture.
- coordinate with the International Variety Testing and Seed
Testing consultants and local consultants to carry out two 10-
day courses, one on seed testing and its management, and
another on field inspection, seed sampling and certification.
- assist in the organization of the a national workshop on
plant variety testing and protection in phase III.

International Seed Law and PVP Specialist
Location.        Beijing with some field travel
Duration.        Two months, one month during each visit.
Oualifications: The consultant should have a law degree and formal graduate
qualification in agriculture or plant sciences, and have more
than 10 year working in the industry in several countries and
have experience in seed and plant breeder right legislation,
UPOV convention, plant breeding and ISTA accredited seed
testing station. Previous developing country and Chinese
experience are preferred.
Duties:         Working in cooperation with the seed law drafting committee
and the Plant Variety Protection Drafting Committee, the
consultant shall:
- review and discuss the draft seed law and plant variety
protection regulation taking the Chinese situation into
consideration.
- provide insight in areas that need improvement in order to
facilitate completion of the drafts.
- assist in designing a plant variety protection (PVP)
implementation system that is appropriate for China.
- assist in preparing an initial list of protected species.
- assist China in its attempt to join the International Seed
Testing Associations (ISTA).
- carry out a follow-up visit in the second year to assist in
implementation.
